      <p>For Earth Day 2017, Earth Day Network launched the goal of global environmental and climate literacy by 2020. EDN envisioned a world that is fluent in the concepts of climate change and aware of its unprecedented threat to our planet. Environmental and climate literacy is the engine not only for creating green voters and advancing environmental and climate laws and policies, but also for accelerating green technologies and jobs. </p>
      <p>To that end, the 2017 Earth Day theme is environmental and climate education. EDN knows that education is the foundation for progress. Before we can solve the dire environmental threats facing us in the 21st century, we must build a global citizenry knowledgeable in environmental science and fluent in local and global ecological issues. A world with a more educated populace internalizes values – such as environmental protection – and is empowered to act in defense of these values. </p>
      <p>To support this Earth Day theme, EDN promoted teach-ins as an activity to educate communities on global environmental issues and how global environmental issues impact local communities. EDN teach-ins strove to empower attendees with real, tangible actions they could take for the environment. </p>
      <p>EDN developed an extensive global outreach strategy to promote Earth Day and assist organizations with producing a variety of actions, including teach-ins, in their own communities. Staff sent thousands of emails and made hundreds of phone calls, and revamped the organization's social media. Additionally, EDN created five teach-in toolkits, with accompanying translations in four languages, to help constituencies organize and mobilize their communities. </p>
      <p>Finally, EDN hosted the flagship March for Science march, rally, and teach-ins on Earth Day on the Washington Monument Grounds in Washington D.C. This event rallied and empowered attendees to support science and evidence-based policy. Approximately 100,000 people attended. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_2018">Earth Day 2018</span></h3> 
      <p>Earth Day 2018’s theme, End Plastic Pollution, was dedicated to building a world of educated citizens who understand the environmental, climate, and health consequences of using plastic.<sup id="cite_ref-:88_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:88-110">[110]</a></sup> Through an online Plastics Pollution Calculator, consumers calculated how much disposable plastic they used in a year and planned how to reduce this amount of waste.<sup id="cite_ref-:89_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:89-111">[111]</a></sup> A Plastic Pollution Primer and Action Toolkit also educated consumers about actions to reduce their plastic footprint. Events worldwide in The Gambia, Italy, Thailand, Japan, India, the U.S., among others, included plastic cleanups, teach-ins, and festivals in which 10,000 partners participated.<sup id="cite_ref-:90_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:90-112">[112]</a></sup> In April 2018, the Google search for “Plastic Pollution” saw the highest trends in the previous five years, 5.5 million pages in 17 languages were created on the internet about “Earth Day 2018” and “plastics,” and global media outlets with a combined audience of 450+ million people covered the campaign. The phrase “plastic pollution” on social media in the U.S. alone reached more than 155 million people. As a result, over 23,0000+ plastic cleanups were registered on Google, 60 countries introduced single-use plastic bans and legislation, and companies such as Coca-Cola and Starbucks announced steps to eliminate and significantly reduce plastic pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-:91_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:91-113">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_2019">Earth Day 2019</span></h3> 
      <p>Earth Day 2019’s theme was Protect Our Species. For this campaign, events and programs spread information about the causes and consequences of growing species extinctions.<sup id="cite_ref-:92_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:92-114">[114]</a></sup> Earth Day Network partnered with <a href="/wiki/Keep_America_Beautiful" title="Keep America Beautiful">Keep America Beautiful</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Cleanup_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="National Cleanup Day">National Cleanup Day</a> for the inaugural nationwide Earth Day Clean Up. Cleanups were held in all 50 States, 5 U.S. Territories, 5,300 sites and had more than 500,000 volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-:93_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:93-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:94_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:94-116">[116]</a></sup> Thousands of locations featured ads with vivid photos of important species. Viewers were encouraged to share photos of ads on social media with the tag #ProtectOurSpecies.<sup id="cite_ref-:95_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:95-117">[117]</a></sup> Earth Day 2019 also encouraged participants to protect threatened species through educational resources, tree plantings, and a climate action guide.<sup id="cite_ref-:96_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:96-118">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span id="Earth_Day_2020.E2.80.932030"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_2020–2030">Earth Day 2020–2030</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_2020">Earth Day 2020</span></h3> 
      <p>Earth Day 2020 was the 50th Anniversary of Earth Day. As marches and gatherings were canceled due to the COVID pandemic — including a large scale event on the National Mall in Washington, D.C. — Earth Day quickly pivoted from mobilizing millions on the ground to raising hundreds of millions of voices digitally to address urgent threats.<sup id="cite_ref-:97_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:97-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:98_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:98-120">[120]</a></sup> Over 100 million people took action in 192 countries to honor Earth Day’s 50th Anniversary in what is being referred to as the largest online mass mobilization in history.<sup id="cite_ref-:99_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:99-121">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Earth Day Network and the <a href="/wiki/Future_Coalition" title="Future Coalition">Future Coalition</a> organized <a href="/wiki/Earth_Day_Live" title="Earth Day Live">Earth Day Live</a>, a three-day livestream event which ran from 9 a.m. to 9 p.m. ET on April 22, 23 and 24.<sup id="cite_ref-:100_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:100-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:101_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:101-123">[123]</a></sup> The event featured speakers from all corners of the environmental movement, youth leaders, A-list celebrities, and global voices. Pope Francis, Secretary General of the UN Antonio Guterres, mayors around the world, Sec. John Kerry, Vice President Al Gore, Ministers of the Environment from multiple countries, Sen. Elizabeth Warren, Sen. Ed Markey, Prince Albert of Monaco – all joined in.<sup id="cite_ref-:102_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:102-124">[124]</a></sup> Governments, municipalities, and corporations made bold new commitments.<sup id="cite_ref-:103_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:103-125">[125]</a></sup> The event also saw performances by musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews" title="Dave Matthews">Dave Matthews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ziggy_Marley" title="Ziggy Marley">Ziggy Marley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Mraz" title="Jason Mraz">Jason Mraz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ang%C3%A9lique_Kidjo" title="Angélique Kidjo">Angélique Kidjo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emily_Wells" title="Emily Wells">Emily Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aimee_Mann" title="Aimee Mann">Aimee Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Leo" title="Ted Leo">Ted Leo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson" class="mw-disambig" title="Jack Johnson">Jack Johnson</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Disambiguation/Fixing_links" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Disambiguation/Fixing links"><span title="Link needs disambiguation (March 2021)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Questlove" title="Questlove">Questlove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-:104_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:104-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:105_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:105-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The series “We Don’t Have Time,” broadcast from Stockholm, Sweden, featured top experts on climate change including Professor Jeffrey Sachs; Christiana Figueres; Johan Rockstrom and Nick Robins as well as youth entrepreneurs and activists.<sup id="cite_ref-:106_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:106-128">[128]</a></sup> The UN Convention on Climate Change also promoted Earth Day 2020 through videos, social media posts and messages under the theme Climate Actors Message, including Executive Secretary Patricia Espinosa; COP25 and Chile Environment Minister Carolina Schmidt; Helena Hemersson, the CEO of H&amp;M and Nigel Topping, the COP26 UK Climate Champion.<sup id="cite_ref-:107_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:107-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Earth Day 2020 was a major topic across media platforms, including leading magazines and environmental publications such as Parade Magazine and The Times of India; television stations such as CBS and CNN; and many more.<sup id="cite_ref-:108_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:108-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:109_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:109-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:110_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:110-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:111_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:111-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:112_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:112-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:113_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:113-135">[135]</a></sup> On January 5, 2020, Earth Day’s 50th anniversary year began with a full page in the <i>Sunday New York Times</i>, referencing a similar black and white advertisement that appeared in the Times 50 years earlier on the first Sunday in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-:114_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:114-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Through social media, Earth Day participants joined digital events and shared their support.<sup id="cite_ref-:115_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:115-137">[137]</a></sup> Through Instagram, HRH The Prince of Wales reminded followers that nature is vital to human health and wellbeing.<sup id="cite_ref-:116_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:116-138">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>“ For fifty years, since the very first Earth Day, I have dedicated a large part of my life to championing more balanced sustainable approaches whether in farming, forestry, fisheries, urban planning or corporate social responsibility. But as we look to shape the next fifty years, I very much need your help. To reflect and inspire the world to action, while aiming for a green recovery, I would ask you to join me by sharing your vision for a more sustainable future (socially, environmentally and economically) using the hashtag ReimagineReset.'.” </p>
      <p>Earth Day 2020 featured programs on education, faith, plastic cleanup, citizen science, reforestation, conservation, food and agriculture, art, green cities and voter mobilization. Acting both globally and locally, Earth Day followers worked to spread climate literacy, end plastic pollution, adopt plant-based diets, preserve biodiversity, and reforest the earth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_2021">Earth Day 2021</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_(02).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_%2802%29.jpg/220px-President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_%2802%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_%2802%29.jpg/330px-President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_%2802%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_%2802%29.jpg/440px-President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_%2802%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Joe_Biden_at_the_Leaders_Summit_on_Climate_(02).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> addresses the Leaders Summit on Climate
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Earth Day 2021 theme is Restore Our Earth and features five primary programs: The Canopy Project, Food and Environment, Climate Literacy, the Global Earth Challenge, and The Great Global CleanUp.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> During the week of Earth Day, EARTHDAY.ORG and lead organizers, Education International, Hip Hop Caucus, and Earth Uprising organized three separate parallel climate action summits on climate literacy, environmental justice, and youth-led climate-focused issues. EARTHDAY.ORG also organized the second-annual Earth Day Live livestream event (April 22, 2021) featuring global activists, international leaders, and influencers.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Biden Administration organized <a href="/w/index.php?title=2021_climate_summit&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2021 climate summit (page does not exist)">a Leaders Summit on Climate on Earth Day 2021</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%BApula_do_Clima_de_2021" class="extiw" title="pt:Cúpula do Clima de 2021">pt</a>]</span>. This virtual <a href="/wiki/Zoom_(software)" title="Zoom (software)">Zoom-like</a> meeting featured 40 world leaders and dozens of speakers, including <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xiye_Bastida" title="Xiye Bastida">Xiye Bastida</a>, Danielle Merfeld, Vice President and Chief Technology Officer, <a href="/wiki/GE_Renewable_Energy" title="GE Renewable Energy">GE Renewable Energy</a>, Anna Borg, President and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Vattenfall" title="Vattenfall">Vattenfall</a>, and Abdullah Subai, Minister of Municipality and Environment, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg/220px-Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg/330px-Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg/440px-Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sure_We_Can_Earthday_clean_2021.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Volunteers at <a href="/wiki/Sure_We_Can" title="Sure We Can">Sure We Can</a> clean McKibbin Street for Earth Day 2021
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_Canada">Earth Day Canada</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11,_1980.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11%2C_1980.jpg/200px-Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11%2C_1980.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11%2C_1980.jpg/300px-Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11%2C_1980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11%2C_1980.jpg/400px-Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11%2C_1980.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="432"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Tinari_Officially_Launching_the_Canadian_First_Earth_Day_on_September_11,_1980.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Paul Tinari officially launched the first Canadian Earth Day on September 11, 1980 – included are <a href="/wiki/Flora_MacDonald_(politician)" title="Flora MacDonald (politician)">Flora MacDonald MP</a>, Ken Keyes and Dr. Ronald Watts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first Canadian Earth Day (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Jour de la Terre</i>) was held on Thursday, September 11, 1980, and was organized by Paul D. Tinari, then a graduate student in Engineering Physics/Solar Engineering at Queen's University. <a href="/wiki/Flora_MacDonald_(politician)" title="Flora MacDonald (politician)">Flora MacDonald</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">MP</a> for <a href="/wiki/Kingston_and_the_Islands" title="Kingston and the Islands">Kingston and the Islands</a> and former Canadian Secretary of State for External Affairs, officially opened Earth Day Week on September 6, 1980, with a ceremonial tree planting and encouraged MPs and <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Provincial_Parliament_(Ontario)" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Provincial Parliament (Ontario)">MPPs</a> across the country to declare a cross-Canada annual Earth Day. The principal activities taking place on the first Earth Day included educational lectures given by experts in various environmental fields, garbage and litter pick-up by students along city roads and highways as well as tree plantings to replace the trees killed by <a href="/wiki/Dutch_elm_disease" title="Dutch elm disease">Dutch elm disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span id="History_of_the_Equinox_Earth_Day_.28March_20.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_Equinox_Earth_Day_(March_20)">History of the Equinox Earth Day (March 20)</span></h2> 
      <p>The equinoctial Earth Day is celebrated on the <a href="/wiki/March_equinox" title="March equinox">March equinox</a> (around March 20) to mark the arrival of astronomical spring in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>, and of astronomical autumn in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">equinox</a> in astronomy is that point in time (not a whole day) when the Sun is directly above the Earth's equator, occurring around March 20 and September 23 each year. In most cultures, the equinoxes and <a href="/wiki/Solstice" title="Solstice">solstices</a> are considered to start or separate the seasons, although weather patterns evolve earlier. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/John_McConnell_(peace_activist)" title="John McConnell (peace activist)">John McConnell</a><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> first introduced the idea of a global holiday called "Earth Day" at the 1969 <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> Conference on the Environment. The first Earth Day <a href="/wiki/Proclamation" title="Proclamation">proclamation</a> was issued by San Francisco Mayor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Alioto" title="Joseph Alioto">Joseph Alioto</a> on March 21, 1970. Celebrations were held in various cities, such as San Francisco and in Davis, California with a multi-day street party. UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a> supported McConnell's global initiative to celebrate this annual event; and on February 26, 1971, he signed a proclamation to that effect, saying:<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>May there be only peaceful and cheerful Earth Days to come for our beautiful <a href="/wiki/Spaceship_Earth" title="Spaceship Earth">Spaceship Earth</a> as it continues to spin and circle in frigid space with its warm and fragile cargo of animate life.</p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>United Nations secretary-general <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Waldheim" title="Kurt Waldheim">Kurt Waldheim</a> observed Earth Day with similar ceremonies on the March equinox in 1972, and the United Nations Earth Day ceremony has continued each year since on the day of the March equinox (the United Nations also works with organizers of the April 22 global event). <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Mead" title="Margaret Mead">Margaret Mead</a> added her support for the equinox Earth Day, and in 1978 declared:<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>Earth Day is the first holy day which transcends all national borders, yet preserves all geographical integrities, spans mountains and oceans and time belts, and yet brings people all over the world into one resonating accord, is devoted to the preservation of the harmony in nature and yet draws upon the triumphs of technology, the measurement of time, and instantaneous communication through space.<br> Earth Day draws on astronomical phenomena in a new way – which is also the most ancient way – by using the Vernal Equinox, the time when the Sun crosses the equator making the length of night and day equal in all parts of the Earth. To this point in the annual calendar, EARTH DAY attaches no local or divisive set of symbols, no statement of the truth or superiority of one way of life over another. But the selection of the March Equinox makes planetary observance of a shared event possible, and a flag which shows the Earth, as seen from space, appropriate.</p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>At the moment of the equinox, it is traditional to observe Earth Day by ringing the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Peace_Bell" title="Japanese Peace Bell">Japanese Peace Bell</a>, which was donated by Japan to the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Over the years, celebrations have occurred in various places worldwide at the same time as the UN celebration. On March 20, 2008, in addition to the ceremony at the United Nations, ceremonies were held in New Zealand, and bells were sounded in California, Vienna, Paris, Lithuania, Tokyo, and many other locations. The equinox Earth Day at the UN is organized by the Earth Society Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Earth Day ringing the peace bell is celebrated around the world in many towns, ringing the Peace Bell in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, and elsewhere. A memorable event took place at the UN in Geneva, celebrating a Minute for Peace ringing the Japanese Shinagawa Peace Bell with the help of the Geneva Friendship Association and the Global Youth Foundation,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> directly after in deep mourning about the <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant">Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant</a> catastrophe 10 days before. </p>
      <p>Beside the Spring Equinox for the Northern Hemisphere, the observance of the Spring Equinox for the Southern Hemisphere in September is of equal importance. The International Day of Peace<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> is celebrated on September 21, and can thus be considered to accord with the original intentions of <a href="/wiki/John_McConnell_(peace_activist)" title="John McConnell (peace activist)">John McConnell</a>, <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a> and others. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="April_22_observances">April 22 observances</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growing_eco-activism_before_Earth_Day_1970">Growing eco-activism before Earth Day 1970</span></h3> 
      <p>In 1968, <a href="/wiki/Morton_Hilbert" title="Morton Hilbert">Morton Hilbert</a> and the U.S. Public Health Service organized the Human Ecology Symposium, an environmental conference for students to hear from scientists about the effects of <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a> on human health.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> This was the beginning of Earth Day. For the next two years, Hilbert and students worked to plan the first Earth Day.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> In April 1970—along with a federal proclamation from U.S. Sen. <a href="/wiki/Gaylord_Nelson" title="Gaylord Nelson">Gaylord Nelson</a>—the first Earth Day was held.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Project_Survival" title="Project Survival">Project Survival</a>, an early environmentalism-awareness education event, was held at <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a> on January 23, 1970. This was the first of several events held at university campuses across the United States in the lead-up to the first Earth Day. Also, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">Ralph Nader</a> began talking about the importance of ecology in 1970. </p>
      <p>The 1960s had been a very dynamic period for ecology in the US. Pre-1960 grassroots activism against <a href="/wiki/DDT" title="DDT">DDT</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_New_York" title="Nassau County, New York">Nassau County</a>, New York, and widespread opposition to open-air <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_testing" title="Nuclear weapons testing">nuclear weapons tests</a> with their global <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fallout" title="Nuclear fallout">nuclear fallout</a>, had inspired <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Carson" title="Rachel Carson">Rachel Carson</a> to write her influential bestseller, <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Spring" title="Silent Spring">Silent Spring</a></i> (1962). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Significance_of_April_22">Significance of April 22</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg/250px-NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg/375px-NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg/500px-NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1056"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NASA-14147-EarthDay20140422-GlobalSelfie-20140522.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Global <a href="/wiki/Selfie" title="Selfie">selfie</a> – Earth Day, April 22, 2014.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nelson chose the date to maximize participation on college campuses for what he conceived as an "environmental teach-in". He determined the week of April 19–25 was the best bet as it did not fall during exams or spring breaks.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Moreover, it did not conflict with religious holidays such as Easter or Passover, and was late enough in spring to have decent weather. More students were likely to be in class, and there would be less competition with other mid-week events—so he chose Wednesday, April 22. The day also fell after the anniversary of the birth of noted conservationist <a href="/wiki/John_Muir" title="John Muir">John Muir</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Muir_National_Historic_Site" title="John Muir National Historic Site">John Muir National Historic Site</a>, has a celebration every year on or around Earth Day (April 21, 22 or 23), called Birthday-Earth Day, in recognition of Earth Day and John Muir's contribution to the collective consciousness of environmentalism and conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unbeknownst to Nelson,<sup id="cite_ref-NelsonCampbell2002_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NelsonCampbell2002-160">[160]</a></sup> April 22, 1970, was coincidentally the <a href="/wiki/Century" title="Century">100th anniversary</a> of the birth of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>, when translated to the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a> (which the Soviets adopted in 1918). <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> reported that some suspected the date was not a coincidence, but a clue that the event was "a Communist trick", and quoted a member of the <a href="/wiki/Daughters_of_the_American_Revolution" title="Daughters of the American Revolution">Daughters of the American Revolution</a> as saying, "subversive elements plan to make American children live in an environment that is good for them."<sup id="cite_ref-time-memento_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-memento-161">[161]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover" title="J. Edgar Hoover">J. Edgar Hoover</a>, director of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a>, may have found the Lenin connection intriguing; it was alleged the FBI conducted surveillance at the 1970 demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The idea that the date was chosen to celebrate Lenin's centenary still persists in some quarters,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> an idea borne out by the similarity with the <a href="/wiki/Subbotnik" title="Subbotnik">subbotnik</a> instituted by Lenin in 1920 as days on which people would have to do community service, which typically consisted in removing rubbish from public property and collecting recyclable material. Subbotniks were also imposed on other countries within the compass of Soviet power, including Eastern Europe, and at the height of its power the Soviet Union established a nationwide subbotnik to be celebrated on Lenin's birthday, April 22, which had been proclaimed a national holiday celebrating communism by <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> in 1955. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day_songs">Earth Day songs</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Earth_Anthem" class="mw-redirect" title="Earth Anthem">Earth Anthem</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are many songs that are performed on Earth Day, that generally fall into two categories: popular songs by contemporary artists not specific to Earth Day that are under copyright or new lyrics adapted to children's songs. </p>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation news cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sevendaysvt.com/vermont/meet-the-79-year-old-man-who-will-oversee-vermonts-energy-future/Content?oid=6217738">"Meet the 79-Year-Old Man Who Will Oversee Vermont's Energy Future"</a>. sevendaysvt.com<span class="reference-accessdate">.            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation news cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/20/climate/denis-hayes-earth-day-organizer.html">"The 'Profoundly Radical' Message of Earth Day's First Organizer"</a>. nytimes.com.          <li id="cite_note-:19-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:19_22-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">McCloskey’s Congressional district included Stanford, where Hayes had been student body president the previous year, and Hayes was friends with Fred Dutton and with Professor Paul Ehrlich who served on the Teach-In’s governing board.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-:0-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-:0_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-:0_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFEditors" class="citation web cs1">Editors, History com. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/the-first-earth-day">"The first Earth Day"</a>. <i>HISTORY</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">April 22,</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=HISTORY&amp;rft.atitle=The+first+Earth+Day&amp;rft.aulast=Editors&amp;rft.aufirst=History+com&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.history.com%2Fthis-day-in-history%2Fthe-first-earth-day&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEarth+Day" class="Z3988"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment">CS1 maint: extra text: authors list (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_extra_text:_authors_list" title="Category:CS1 maint: extra text: authors list">link</a>)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-:20-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:20_24-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nan Robertson. <i>Angry Coordinator of Earth Day,</i> New York Times, April 22, 1970</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-:21-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:21_25-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://adage.com/article/special-report-the-advertising-century/ad-age-advertising-century-top-100-campaigns/140918">https://adage.com/article/special-report-the-advertising-century/ad-age-advertising-century-top-100-campaigns/140918</a>. To the careful observer, the values that underpinned the VW ads actually were aligned with many of the values of Earth Day. The Think Small campaign rebutted the industry’s preoccupation with conspicuous consumption with what might be termed “conspicuous frugality.” The ads were dismissive of massive V-8 engines, tailfins, and bushels of chrome. They took pride in high mileage, low maintenance. They viewed cars as transportation, not status symbols.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-:22-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:22_26-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Senator Nelson did not initially care for the change, and he continued to insist on calling the event Environmental Teach-In through April. Ultimately, however, Nelson too adopted the new name and later took enormous pride in being termed the father of Earth Day.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-:23-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:23_27-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One consequence of leaving the name in the public domain was that bad actors could use it as well. Over time, major corporate polluters, rapacious timber operators, oil companies, and other bad environmental actors have run their own Earth Day campaigns, often leading to public misperceptions that they are funding or otherwise aligned with the Earth Day Network. </span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-:24-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:24_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hamilton had earlier worked for Save the Children. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.savethechildren.org/">https://www.savethechildren.org/</a></span> </li>

Earth Day Network</a>. Retrieved August 16, 2013.</span> </li>

      <p><br> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Day">Earth Day</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.earthday.org/">Earth Day Network</a> – Coordinating worldwide events for Earth Day</li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://cleanup.earthday.org/">The Great Global CleanUp</a> – CleanUp Website including Global Map, Signup to CleanUp and Find a CleanUp</li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.epa.gov/earthday/">United States Earth Day</a> – The U.S. government's <i>Earth Day</i> site</li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.earthday.ca/">Earth Day Canada</a> – The Canadian Official Site for <i>Earth Day</i></li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.history.com/topics/earth-day">Earth Day</a> at The History Channel</li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nelsonearthday.net/">Gaylord Nelson and Earth Day: The Making of the Modern Environmental Movement</a> narrative account of the origins of Earth Day, Nelson's political career, as well as online access to documents from the Wisconsin Historical Society's Nelson Papers collection</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Equinoctial_Earth_Day">Equinoctial Earth Day</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://earthsocietyfoundation.com/">Earth Society Foundation</a> – Official organization arranging annual equinox Earth Day celebration at the United Nations</li>
      </ul>

            Legend: 
            <p>(federal) = federal holidays, (abbreviation) = state/territorial holidays, (religious) = religious holidays, (cultural) = holiday related to a specific <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">racial/ethnic group</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sexual_minority" title="Sexual minority">sexual minority</a>, (week) = week-long holidays, (month) = month-long holidays, (36) = <a href="/wiki/Title_36_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 36 of the United States Code">Title 36 Observances and Ceremonies</a><br> <b>Bold</b> indicates major holidays commonly celebrated in the United States, which often represent the major celebrations of the month.<br> </p> See also: <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_holidays" title="Lists of holidays">Lists of holidays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hallmark_holiday" title="Hallmark holiday">Hallmark holidays</a>, public holidays in the <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_United_States" title="Public holidays in the United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_holidays_in_New_Jersey" title="State holidays in New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_government_holidays" title="New York State government holidays">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Public holidays in Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Public holidays in the United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>.
